{"uri": "8095663066", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-04-24", "time": "21:50:38", "dateTime": "2024-04-24T21:50:38Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-04-24T21:49:55Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6274510025978088, "url": "https://www.cleveland.com/browns/2024/04/browns-final-mock-roundup-shows-variety-ahead-of-2024-nfl-draft.html", "title": "Browns' final mock roundup shows variety ahead of 2024 NFL Draft", "body": "CLEVELAND, Ohio -- Barring any trades, the Browns will officially be on the clock in the 2024 NFL Draft about 48 hours from now, and in a final roundup of mock drafts, it seems like most analysts are in agreement: Just about anything is possible for Cleveland at pick No. 54.\n\nAnd it makes sense: That's just the nature of drafting that late in the second round, with the Browns officially in their final draft without a first-round pick due to the Deshaun Watson trade. Everything has to be on the table, because it's too hard to gauge exactly what might happen in the 53 picks before.\n\nThat being said, here's a final round of names analysts had available for the Browns:\n\nNFL.com's Chad Reuter stays with Cooper in this pick, who he had coming to Cleveland in his last multi-round mock as well.\n\nIn 2023, Cooper was a first-team AP All-American and first-team All-SEC selection. He led the team with 84 tackles, 17 TFL, 8.0 sacks, tied for team lead with two forced fumbles, and also had two pass breakups.\n\n\"Highly physical linebacker with elite top-end speed and a burning desire to get to the football that can lead to some inconsistencies in his play,\" writes NFL analyst Lance Zierlein. \"Cooper is average at diagnosing the run but takes off around traffic on a mission to find the ball-carrier once he sees it. He can be undisciplined playing his run fits and takes unorthodox paths downhill, but he somehow finds ways to slither around blocks and make challenging tackles.\"\n\nIf there's one thing the Browns love, it's drafting DBs.\n\nThe Bleacher Report Scouting Department has them pegged with adding to one of their most obvious strengths.\n\nIn 2023, Lassiter earned second-team All-SEC honors for the Bulldogs. He started all 14 games and led the team with 8 pass breakups.\n\nCBS Sports' Ryan Wilson has the Browns adding some more depth to their interior line. On a team that doesn't have a ton of \"needs\" necessarily, the interior line is certainly one of them after Jordan Elliott departed in free agency.\n\n\"This Browns defense was dominant for much of last season and Hall is a twitched-up terror who was consistently disruptive for the Buckeyes a year ago,\" Wilson writes. \"He only weighed 290 at the combine, but that's in the same range as Shelby Harris and Maurice Hurst.\"\n\nHall had a pretty good Senior Bowl showing, and ended the 2023 season with third-team All-Big Ten accolades. There have certainly been trends -- age matters in many cases and trading down is always on the table -- but it hasn't been easy to put Berry in a box.\n\nThis is the final draft with no first-round picks as a result of the Deshaun Watson trade and Berry has kept the roster afloat. The biggest question mark, ironically, might be quarterback.\n\nThe Browns don't go on the clock until Friday night, but they'll be active once their turn gets close. Here are three predictions for this weekend.\n\nBerry has traded up before and it was in a similar spot to where the Browns are in this draft. In 2021, Berry moved from No. 59 to No. 52 to select linebacker Jeremiah Owusu-Koramoah. Along with No. 59, he swapped the No. 89 pick for the No. 113 pick, moving from the end of the third to the beginning of the fourth.\n\n\"In reality, you probably get a more narrow focus maybe 10 -- call it 10 picks out,\" Berry said in his pre-draft press conference last week, \"because that's when really players become, I guess, more in striking distance.\"\n\nIt all will depend on how the draft shakes out once the Browns get within striking distance, but it wouldn't be a surprise if Berry manufactured a deal similar to the trade up he used to get Owusu-Koramoah. The Browns had two third-round picks to utilize then, but if the right player is there, it might be worth trading out of Saturday night if needed, especially considering they don't have a fourth-round pick and would probably like one, even if it came at the expense of No. 85.\n\nIf we were placing odds, a trade down would be the favorite, but the template exists for a small move up. Don't bet against it.\n\nBerry tends to not leave many needs for the draft to fill, especially when he hasn't had a first-round pick. One example was in 2020 when they didn't address left tackle prior to the draft and selected Jedrick Wills Jr. at No. 10.\n\nA glance at the current roster doesn't show many glaring needs -- they could use another linebacker, perhaps, and some more depth at defensive tackle, but for the most part the top of the roster is in good shape.\n\nWhen you dig in behind David Njoku at tight end, there might be an opportunity for a young player. Right now it's Jordan Akins, Giovanni Ricci and Zaire Mitchell-Paden. The departure of Harrison Bryant left TE2 open for competition.\n\nThe Browns selected Bryant to start Day 3 in 2020 and if they manage to land a fourth-round pick somehow, a tight end could be in consideration.\n\nBerry recently acquired a second seventh-round pick and while those haven't always been picks he's kept, you only have to go back two years to find a draft where he made two seventh-round picks.\n\n\"It's a trade that we thought could give us a resource that we could use effectively,\" Berry said last week of adding a seventh. \"How we deploy that resource remains to be seen. It could be we could select players with those two picks. It could be part of a move up.\"\n\nThe bottom of the roster became a little more important when the NFL changed the kickoff rule for this season. More returns means more players who need to be able to cover kicks and do it in a different way.\n\n\"I think the body type for kickoff coverage players is going to potentially change pretty significantly,\" Berry said. \"Because you're taking a lot of speed and space out of the traditional play. I think you're going to probably see bigger body types, guys that are really good with their hands and that can, I would say, traditionally get off blocks as opposed to maybe use their speed and quickness to avoid a block just because of the setup rules.\"\n\nLate draft picks and undrafted free agents have to thrive on special teams to make it in the league and Berry could find value in using at least one of those seventh-rounders on a player who could start out contributing in a big way on Bubba Ventrone's coverage units.", "source": {"uri": "cleveland.com", "dataType": "news", "title": {"uri": "8096807837", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-04-25", "time": "13:17:39", "dateTime": "2024-04-25T13:17:39Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-04-25T13:16:25Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.4745098054409027, "url": "https://brownswire.usatoday.com/lists/browns-2024-nfl-draft-tvondre-sweat-troy-franklin-players-to-avoid/", "title": "5 2024 NFL draft prospects the Browns should avoid", "body": "We have arrived. The 2024 NFL draft starts today, and while the Cleveland Browns do not have a first round pick, you better believe they have done their homework on Troy Franklin, T'Vondre Sweat, and other potential Day 2 targets.\n\nWith team needs along their offensive line, at wide receiver, defensive tackle, and linebacker, the Browns could go in a variety of directions on Friday night. While players like Florida State wide receiver Keon Coleman or BYU offensive tackle Kingsley Suamataia are ideal targets for the Browns to circle in Sharpie, there are also a plethora of players they should have a big red X next to.\n\nHere are five players the Browns must avoid when they come on the clock with pick No. 54, 85 or anywhere else throughout the 2024 NFL draft.\n\nWR Troy Franklin, Oregon\n\nOregon wide receiver Troy Franklin celebrates a touchdown as the No. 6 Oregon Ducks host the USC Trojans Saturday, Nov. 11, 2023, at Autzen Stadium in Eugene, Ore.\n\nThere are way too many question marks about Oregon wide receiver for me to feel good about using a second round pick on him.\n\nI'm worried about his slender 174-pound frame. I'm worried about his ability to consistently track the football down the field. I'm worried about his potential to run a full route tree and not just stride it out on the vertical plane.\n\nCan he play through contact and beat press man coverage? Can he sink his hips and get in and out of breaks on routes that aren't just screens or verticals? Can his body hold up at the NFL level?\n\nHopefully that's not a question the Browns have to answer and someone drafts him earlier than pick No. 54.\n\nTE Ja'Tavion Sanders, Texas\n\nTexas Longhorns wide receiver Ja'Tavion Sanders (0) celebrates a catch for a first down during the Big 12 Championship game against the Oklahoma State Cowboys at AT&T stadium on Saturday, Dec. 2, 2023 in Arlington.\n\nFor starters, the guy cannot block worth a lick.\n\nThe calling card of Sanders was supposed to be his mismatch ability in the passing game and his athleticism. It turns out, however, that Sanders is not all that athletic either. While he runs a fast 40-yard dash, his explosiveness testing fell well below par, hitting just 30 inches in the vertical jump and 9-feet-6 in the broad jump.\n\nSanders overlaps and does not compliment the skillset of David Njoku at all. If we are being honest a good comparison for Sanders is Dollar Tree David Njoku (who has developed into one of the better blocking tight ends in the NFL).\n\nWhile the Browns need another tight end, and will probably look hard in the 2024 NFL draft for one, Sanders is not the one to go after.\n\nDL Brandon Dorlus, Oregon\n\nSep 17, 2022; Eugene, Oregon, USA; Oregon Ducks defensive end Brandon Dorlus (3) celebrates after a defensive stop against the Brigham Young Cougars at Autzen Stadium. Oregon won the game 41-20. Mandatory Credit: Troy Wayrynen-USA TODAY Sports\n\nWhat do you do with Brandon Dorlus along your defensive line?\n\nHe is too small to play three-tech but not athletic enough to win on the edge. He weighed in at just 283 pounds (21st percentile among all defensive tackles historically) and does not show the play strength on tape to two-gap, anchor doubles, or win with ease from the interior. However, if you run his testing numbers as a defensive end, Dorlus is just a 45th-percentile athlete there.\n\nA true tweener, Dorlus is a hard man to find a role for in an NFL defense. It's particularly hard to pinpoint a pathway to the field in Jim Schwartz's defensive scheme in Cleveland.\n\nLB Jeremiah Trotter Jr., Clemson\n\nSep 16, 2023; Clemson, South Carolina; Clemson linebacker Jeremiah Trotter Jr. (54) tackles Florida Atlantic running back Zuberi Mobley (2) the third quarter with Florida Atlantic at Memorial Stadium. Mandatory Credit: Ken Ruinard-USA TODAY NETWORK\n\nNepotism will take you a long way in the NFL, and Clemson linebacker Jeremiah Trotter Jr. has been a big beneficiary of it this year. Despite being undersized and unathletic, Trotter Jr. constantly gets mock drafted on Day 2 of these exercises.\n\nThen when looking at his tape, Trotter Jr.'s eyes are constantly in the wrong spot, forcing his teammates to correct. The Browns need a linebacker, but Trotter Jr. is not the one to go after. When grading Trotter, he is far closer to grading out as an undrafted free agent than he is as a Day 2 pick. However, he may be a benefactor from the sheer low number of players entering the draft this year.\n\nLet another team make that pick.\n\nDT T'Vondre Sweat, Texas\n\nFeb 29, 2024; Indianapolis, IN, USA; Texas defensive lineman T'Vondre Sweat (DL25) works out during the 2024 NFL Combine at Lucas Oil Stadium. Mandatory Credit: Kirby Lee-USA TODAY Sports\n\nAfter drafting Siaki Ika last year, another massive-bodied defensive tackle who did not fit the gap-shooting tasks that Schwartz asks of his defensive tackles, why would the Browns do that again this year with Texas defensive tackle T'Vondre Sweat?\n\nNot to mention the murmurs that he played in 2023 around 390 pounds, the DWI two weeks before the draft, and is overall athleticism.\n\nIf the Browns look for another defensive tackle, which is a real possibility with two of the guys in their current room on one-year deals, they are better off going after guys who can shoot gaps and penetrate against the pass at a higher level.
